# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes CNI Network Plugin Interface Architecture

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the CNI (Container Network Interface) integration: the CNI plugin invocation, the network namespace setup, the IP address management (IPAM) call, and the network plugin manager that coordinates CNI calls during pod creation.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Summary of CNI-Related Files in Kubernetes v1.32.0

Based on my comprehensive search of the kubernetes/kubernetes repository (github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes), here are all the key files related to CNI (Container Network Interface) integration:

### 1. **Pod Sandbox Creation and Network Setup**

#### /workspace/pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go
- **Purpose**: Core pod sandbox creation logic
- **Key Functions**: `createPodSandbox()`, `generatePodSandboxConfig()`
- **CNI Role**: Generates sandbox configuration and invokes the CRI RuntimeService.RunPodSandbox() which triggers CNI plugin execution

#### /workspace/pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox_linux.go
- **Purpose**: Linux-specific pod sandbox setup
- **Key Functions**: `applySandboxResources()`, `calculateSandboxResources()`
- **CNI Role**: Handles Linux resource configuration for sandbox network setup

#### /workspace/pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox_windows.go
- **Purpose**: Windows-specific pod sandbox setup

#### /workspace/pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/util/util.go
- **Purpose**: Utility functions for sandbox/pod setup
- **Key Functions**: `NetworkNamespaceForPod()`, namespace mode determination for pods
- **CNI Role**: Determines if a pod uses host network namespace or pod namespace

---

#### /workspace/pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network.go
- **Purpose**: Kubelet network configuration interface
- **Key Functions**: `updatePodCIDR()`, `providerRequiresNetworkingConfiguration()`, `GetPodDNS()`
- **CNI Role**: Manages pod CIDR updates and DNS configuration, bridges kubelet to runtime network plugins

Perfect! I've successfully created a comprehensive answer file documenting all the Go source files in Kubernetes v1.32.0 that implement CNI (Container Network Interface) integration. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

**16 core files identified** implementing CNI integration:

### Pod Sandbox & Network Setup (4 files)
- `kuberuntime_sandbox.go` - Core CNI plugin invocation via `createPodSandbox()`
- `kuberuntime_sandbox_linux.go` - Linux-specific network resource setup
- `kuberuntime_sandbox_windows.go` - Windows/HNS integration
- `kuberuntime_manager.go` - Pod lifecycle orchestration

### Network Management (3 files)
- `kubelet_network.go` - Pod CIDR management, DNS configuration
- `kubelet_network_linux.go` - Linux network utilities
- `kubelet_network_others.go` - Platform-agnostic utilities

### CRI Integration (2 files)
- `container/runtime.go` - Abstract Runtime interface for CNI
- `instrumented_services.go` - Monitoring wrapper for CNI calls

### IP Address Management (4 files)
- `node_ipam_controller.go` - Node-level CIDR allocation
- `cidr_allocator.go` - CIDR allocation strategy interface
- `range_allocator.go` - Range-based CIDR allocator
- `cidrset/cidr_set.go` - CIDR tracking data structure

### Network Statistics (3 files)
- `cri_stats_provider.go` - Network stats collection
- `cri_stats_provider_linux.go` - Linux network stats
- `cri_stats_provider_windows.go` - Windows network stats

The answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` contains complete details including specific symbols and the call chain showing how `syncPod()` triggers `createPodSandbox()` which invokes the CRI runtime to execute CNI plugins.

CNI Network Plugin Integration Architecture (v1.32.0)\\n\\n### Overview\\nThe CNI (Container Network Interface) integration in Kubernetes v1.32.0 is implemented through a layered architecture where the kubelet delegates network setup to the CRI (Container Runtime Interface) runtime, which in turn invokes CNI plugins.\\n\\n### Core CNI Plugin Invocation Flow\\n\\n**1. Pod Sandbox Creation and Network Setup**\\n- **pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go**: `createPodSandbox()` function initiates pod sandbox creation. This function calls `generatePodSandboxConfig()` to build the pod sandbox configuration and then invokes `runtimeService.RunPodSandbox()` which delegates to the CRI runtime (containerd/CRI-O) to execute CNI plugins.\\n- **pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox_linux.go**: Contains Linux-specific sandbox setup logic including resource configuration (`applySandboxResources()`, `calculateSandboxResources()`) that affects network resource allocation.\\n- **pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox_windows.go**: Provides Windows-specific sandbox configuration for HNS (Host Networking Service) integration.\\n- **pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go**: The `kubeGenericRuntimeManager` orchestrates pod lifecycle. The `syncPod()` function calls `createPodSandbox()` with error handling that catches CNI-related failures (errors are explicitly noted as coming from \\\"CNI, CSI\\\").\\n\\n### Network Namespace Setup and Management\\n\\n**2. Network Namespace Configuration**\\n- **pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network.go**: Provides the kubelet's network interface for managing pod networking:\\n  - `updatePodCIDR()`: Updates the pod CIDR in runtime state and delegates to the runtime via `getRuntime().UpdatePodCIDR()` which propagates to network plugins\\n  - `providerRequiresNetworkingConfiguration()`: Determines if cloud provider requires special networking (checks for GCE provider with Routes() interface)\\n  - `GetPodDNS()`: Retrieves DNS configuration for pods through `dnsConfigurer.GetPodDNS()`\\n  \\n- **pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network_linux.go**: Linux-specific network utilities for pod networking setup\\n\\n- **pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network_others.go**: Platform-agnostic network utilities\\n\\n### Container Runtime Interface (CRI) Integration\\n\\n**3. CRI Runtime Service Abstraction**\\n- **pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go**: Defines the abstract `Runtime` interface that all container runtimes must implement. The interface includes methods like `RunPodSandbox()` which is called with `PodSandboxConfig` containing network configuration. The actual CNI plugin execution happens within the CRI runtime implementation.\\n\\n- **pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/instrumented_services.go**: Provides instrumented wrappers around CRI runtime calls including `RunPodSandbox()`, adding metrics and monitoring for CNI plugin execution.\\n\\n### IP Address Management (IPAM)\\n\\n**4. Node-Level CIDR Allocation**\\n- **pkg/controller/nodeipam/node_ipam_controller.go**: The `Controller` manages IP Address Management at the node level. It coordinates with the cloud provider and allocates CIDR ranges to nodes. The controller runs continuously via its `Run()` method.\\n\\n- **pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/cidr_allocator.go**: Defines the `CIDRAllocator` interface with multiple allocation strategies:\\n  - `RangeAllocatorType`: Allocates from cluster CIDR range\\n  - `CloudAllocatorType`: Allocates from cloud provider\\n  - `IPAMFromClusterAllocatorType`: Syncs cluster allocations to cloud\\n  - `IPAMFromCloudAllocatorType`: Syncs cloud allocations to cluster\\n\\n- **pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/range_allocator.go**: Implements the `rangeAllocator` struct that handles CIDR allocation from cluster CIDR ranges. Key functions include:\\n  - `NewCIDRRangeAllocator()`: Creates allocator with CIDR sets for each cluster CIDR\\n  - `AllocateOrOccupyCIDR()`: Allocates or occupies a CIDR for a node\\n  - `ReleaseCIDR()`: Releases a previously allocated CIDR\\n  - `Run()`: Main controller loop that processes node queue\\n\\n- **pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/cidrset/cidr_set.go**: Implements `CidrSet` data structure for managing individual CIDR block allocations. Tracks which CIDRs are available for allocation and which are in use.\\n\\n### Network Statistics and Monitoring\\n\\n**5. Network Stats Collection**\\n- **pkg/kubelet/stats/cri_stats_provider.go**: Provides statistics for pods/containers including network stats (`listContainerNetworkStats()`)\\n- **pkg/kubelet/stats/cri_stats_provider_linux.go**: Linux-specific network statistics gathering\\n- **pkg/kubelet/stats/cri_stats_provider_windows.go**: Windows-specific network statistics gathering\\n\\n### CNI Integration Flow Summary\\n\\n1. **Pod Creation**: `kubelet.syncPod()` \u2192 `kubeGenericRuntimeManager.syncPod()` \u2192 `createPodSandbox()`\\n2. **Sandbox Config Generation**: `generatePodSandboxConfig()` builds config including network settings\\n3. **CRI Invocation**: `runtimeService.RunPodSandbox()` delegates to CRI runtime (containerd/CRI-O)\\n4. **CNI Plugin Execution**: CRI runtime invokes CNI plugins from `/opt/cni/bin/` with IPAM settings\\n5. **IPAM**: `NodeIPAMController` allocates node CIDR ranges via `CIDRAllocator`\\n6. **Network Setup**: Pod receives IP address from CIDR allocated to node, network namespace is created\\n7. **Pod Network Ready**: DNS configuration is passed to pod, network stats are collected\\n\\n### Key Implementation Details\\n\\n- **Namespace Isolation**: Network namespaces are created by CRI runtime based on pod configuration (host vs pod namespace determined via `generatePodSandboxLinuxConfig()` logic)\\n- **IPAM Strategy**: The allocator type (RangeAllocator, CloudAllocator, etc.) determines how node CIDRs are obtained and managed\\n- **CNI Plugin Parameters**: The PodSandboxConfig passed to RunPodSandbox includes pod metadata, port mappings, and DNS settings that are used by CNI plugins\\n- **Error Handling**: Network setup failures from CNI plugins are caught at `createPodSandbox()` level and propagated as pod creation failures\\n- **Platform Specific**: Separate implementations for Linux (_linux.go), Windows (_windows.go), and platform-agnostic code\\n\\nThe architecture cleanly separates concerns: kubelet handles pod lifecycle and CIDR allocation, while the CRI runtime handles the actual CNI plugin invocation and network namespace management.\"\n}\n",

The controller runs continuously via its `Run()` method.\\n\\n- **pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/cidr_allocator.go**: Defines the `CIDRAllocator` interface with multiple allocation strategies:\\n  - `RangeAllocatorType`: Allocates from cluster CIDR range\\n  - `CloudAllocatorType`: Allocates from cloud provider\\n  - `IPAMFromClusterAllocatorType`: Syncs cluster allocations to cloud\\n  - `IPAMFromCloudAllocatorType`: Syncs cloud allocations to cluster\\n\\n- **pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/range_allocator.go**: Implements the `rangeAllocator` struct that handles CIDR allocation from cluster CIDR ranges. Key functions include:\\n  - `NewCIDRRangeAllocator()`: Creates allocator with CIDR sets for each cluster CIDR\\n  - `AllocateOrOccupyCIDR()`: Allocates or occupies a CIDR for a node\\n  - `ReleaseCIDR()`: Releases a previously allocated CIDR\\n  - `Run()`: Main controller loop that processes node queue\\n\\n- **pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/cidrset/cidr_set.go**: Implements `CidrSet` data structure for managing individual CIDR block allocations. Tracks which CIDRs are available for allocation and which are in use.\\n\\n### Network Statistics and Monitoring\\n\\n**5. Network Stats Collection**\\n- **pkg/kubelet/stats/cri_stats_provider.go**: Provides statistics for pods/containers including network stats (`listContainerNetworkStats()`)\\n- **pkg/kubelet/stats/cri_stats_provider_linux.go**: Linux-specific network statistics gathering\\n- **pkg/kubelet/stats/cri_stats_provider_windows.go**: Windows-specific network statistics gathering\\n\\n### CNI Integration Flow Summary\\n\\n1. **Pod Creation**: `kubelet.syncPod()` \u2192 `kubeGenericRuntimeManager.syncPod()` \u2192 `createPodSandbox()`\\n2. **Sandbox Config Generation**: `generatePodSandboxConfig()` builds config including network settings\\n3. **CRI Invocation**: `runtimeService.RunPodSandbox()` delegates to CRI runtime (containerd/CRI-O)\\n4. **CNI Plugin Execution**: CRI runtime invokes CNI plugins from `/opt/cni/bin/` with IPAM settings\\n5. **IPAM**: `NodeIPAMController` allocates node CIDR ranges via `CIDRAllocator`\\n6. **Network Setup**: Pod receives IP address from CIDR allocated to node, network namespace is created\\n7. **Pod Network Ready**: DNS configuration is passed to pod, network stats are collected\\n\\n### Key Implementation Details\\n\\n- **Namespace Isolation**: Network namespaces are created by CRI runtime based on pod configuration (host vs pod namespace determined via `generatePodSandboxLinuxConfig()` logic)\\n- **IPAM Strategy**: The allocator type (RangeAllocator, CloudAllocator, etc.) determines how node CIDRs are obtained and managed\\n- **CNI Plugin Parameters**: The PodSandboxConfig passed to RunPodSandbox includes pod metadata, port mappings, and DNS settings that are used by CNI plugins\\n- **Error Handling**: Network setup failures from CNI plugins are caught at `createPodSandbox()` level and propagated as pod creation failures\\n- **Platform Specific**: Separate implementations for Linux (_linux.go), Windows (_windows.go), and platform-agnostic code\\n\\nThe architecture cleanly separates concerns: kubelet handles pod lifecycle and CIDR allocation, while the CRI runtime handles the actual CNI plugin invocation and network namespace management.\"\n}\n",
